Inferring the Creator from Observed States and Classifying Bodies
Sanusi presents a method of proving the Creator through observed states and classifies bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the method of inferring the Creator from observed states and the classification of bodies into celestial and elemental, along with their subdivisions.

Core Idea
Observing what humans cannot produce leads to the Creator; all bodies reveal His signs.

This lesson presents two related ideas: first, a direct argument for God's existence based on observable phenomena that humans cannot produce; second, a detailed classification of bodies (celestial and elemental) that serves as the canvas for this argument. The author invites us to see the entire physical world as a source of evidence for the Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening argument
Notice that the author starts from direct observation of states and attributes humans cannot produce, even before debating bodies' possibility. This is a unique starting point.
The phrase 'نشاهد حدوث أحوال وصفات' is key.
2
Identify the two main body classes
The passage divides bodies into celestial (falakiyya) and elemental (ʿunṣuriyya). Understand the basis of this division.
Celestial bodies are the heavens and planets; elemental are the four elements and their compounds.
3
Explore celestial inquiries
Three lines of inquiry about celestial bodies: their motions, day/night and shadows, and planetary positions relative to the zenith. Each shows divine order.
4
Examine elemental simples and compounds
Simples are the four elements; compounds include celestial effects, minerals, plants, and animals. Each level reveals wisdom.
Humans are included in animals but receive special focus.
5
Reflect on the purpose
How does this classification support the inference to the Creator? Each body type provides observable evidence of design and power beyond human capacity.
The method does not require prior proof of contingency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم : أنا قبل العلم بإمكان [ ذوات ] الأجسام وقبل العلم بحدوثها : نشاهد حدوث أحوال وصفات ، لا يقدر البشر عليها . فلا جرم يمكننا أن نستدل بها على وجود الصانع
فاعلم : أن الأجسام التي هي المحال لهذه الحوادث المشاهدة المحسوسة : إما أن تكون هي الأجسام الفلكية ، أو الأجسام العنصرية . أما الأجسام الأفلاك والكواكب. والبحث عنها إما أن يقع في كيفية حركاتها الفلكية فهي ودورانها وطلوع الكواكب وغروبها . وإما أن تقع بحسب الليل والنهار ، واعتبار أحوال الأضواء والإظلال وأما تقع بحسب الأحوال المختلفة التي تعرض للكواكب بسبب قربها أو بعدها من سمت الرؤوس ، وبسبب المصالح الحاصلة من الفصول الأربعة .
وأما الأجسام العنصرية فهي إما بسائط أو مركبات . أما البسائط فالبحث عن أحوال العناصر الأربعة وتركيباتها وصفاتها وكيفية ما أودع الله تعالى فيها من العجائب والمنافع. وأما المركبات فهي أربعة : الآثار العلوية والمعادن والنبات والحيوان والإنسان داخل في الحيوان . والبحث عن الإنسان ، إما عن تشريح بدنه [ لمعرفة ] ما أودع الله فيه من [ الأسرار ] والعجائب والغرائب . وإما عن تشريح القوى النفسانية وأحوالها العجيبة من أنواع إدراكاتها وأفعالها
Know: before knowledge of the possibility of the essences of bodies and before knowledge of their occurrence, we observe the occurrence of states and attributes that humans are incapable of. Therefore, it is possible for us to infer by them the existence of the Maker. Know also: the bodies that are the loci of these observed, sensed events are either celestial bodies or elemental bodies. As for the bodies of the heavens and planets, inquiry into them either concerns how their celestial motions, their rotation, the rising of planets and their setting; or it concerns the night and day, and consideration of the states of lights and shadows; or it concerns the different states that occur to the planets due to their nearness or distance from the zenith, and due to the benefits arising from the four seasons. As for elemental bodies, they are either simple or compound. As for the simples, inquiry concerns the states of the four elements, their compositions, their attributes, and how God Most High has deposited in them wonders and benefits. As for compounds, they are four: celestial effects, minerals, plants, and animals—and humans are included within animals. Inquiry concerning humans is either about the anatomy of his body to know what God has deposited in him of secrets, wonders, and marvels; or about the anatomy of the psychic faculties and their wondrous states, comprising types of their perceptions and actions.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage presents a method of proving the existence of the Creator through the observation of changing states and attributes that humans cannot produce. The author begins by stating that even before we know whether bodies are possible in themselves or whether they are originated, we directly observe changes (ḥudūth aḥwāl wa-ṣifāt) that are beyond human power. These observations alone suffice to infer a Maker. The author then categorizes bodies into two types: celestial (al-ajsām al-falakiyya) and elemental (al-ajsām al-ʿunṣuriyya). For celestial bodies, inquiry can focus on their motions, rotations, risings and settings; or on the alternation of night and day and the states of light and shadow; or on varying planetary positions relative to the zenith and the resulting benefits of the four seasons. For elemental bodies, they are either simple (basāʾiṭ)—the four elements—or compound (murakkabāt). The simples are examined for their states, compositions, attributes, and the wonders and benefits God placed in them. The compounds are four: celestial effects (āthār ʿulwiyya), minerals, plants, and animals (with humans included in animals). Humans are studied either through the anatomy of the body to discover the secrets and wonders deposited by God, or through the anatomy of the psychic faculties and their wondrous perceptions and actions. The entire classification serves to show how each type of body provides observable evidence of divine wisdom and power, forming a rich source of proofs for the Creator.

Correction: The author argues that direct observation of states beyond human capacity suffices without those prior proofs.

The Power of Sensory Proofs: Sensation and Multiplicity
Author lists first two of four reasons for superiority of observable proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first two reasons why proofs based on observable attributes are more impactful: the combination of sensation and imagination, and the certainty gained from multiplicity.

Core Idea
Sensory proofs combine sensation and imagination to dispel doubt, and their abundance yields certainty.

This passage from al-Matālib al-ʿĀliyah explains why proofs based on observable attributes (dalāʾil ḥissiyya) are superior. The author begins by asserting their impact and then gives four reasons. In this lesson, we cover the first two reasons: the role of sensation and imagination, and the power of multiplicity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall meaning.
The passage is concise; note the key terms 'al-ḥiss wa-al-khayāl'.
2
Understand the claim
Notice the author's claim: this type of proof is more impactful in hearts, more effective in minds, and further from doubts.
This sets up why he gives reasons.
3
Examine the first reason
The first reason: sensation and imagination together act as two opposites to the intellect, causing doubts to disappear.
Think about how sensory evidence reinforces intellectual conviction.
4
Examine the second reason
The second reason: these proofs are numerous and diverse; their abundance and succession yield strength and certainty.
Contrast a single proof with multiple converging proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم : أن هذا النوع من الدلائل أوقع في القلوب وأكثر تأثيرا في العقول ، وأبعد عن جهات الشبهات . والسبب فيه . وجوه : الأول : إن في هذا النوع من الدلائل الحس والخيال معا ضدان العقل فتزول الشبهات . والثاني : إنها كثيرة متعارضة بسبب الكثرة ، والتوالي يفيد القوة والجزم . والثالث : إن هذه الأشياء إن كانت دلائل من بعض الوجوه ، فإنها منافع من وجه آخر . والإنسان مجبول على حب المنافع . فكان حبه لها ، وميل طبعه إليها يمنعه من إنكارها، ومن إلقاء الشبهات فيها . والرابع : إنه لا ينفك في شيء من أحواله عن مشاهدة شيء فيها ، ومباشرة قسم من أقسامها . وكثرة الممارسة تفيد الملكة الراسخة . وإذا عرفت هذه الوجوه المقتضية لرجحان هذه الطريقة على سائر الطرق . فنقول : لما كان الأمر كذلك، كانت الكتب الإلهية مملوءة من هذا النوع من الدلائل . لا سيما القرآن العظيم. وكذلك فإنك متى أوردت أنواعاً كثيرة من هذه الدلائل، طابت القلوب ، وخضعت النفوس ، وأذعنت الأفكار ، للإقرار بوجود الإله الحكيم. ومن أراد الاستقصاء فيه . فكأنه لا يتم
And know: this type of proof is more impactful in hearts, more effective in minds, and further from the avenues of doubts. The reason for it has aspects: First: in this type of proof, sensation and imagination together are two opposites to the intellect, so doubts disappear. Second: they are numerous and diverse due to abundance, and succession yields strength and certainty. Third: these things, if they are proofs in some respects, they are benefits in another respect. And humans are naturally disposed to love benefits. So their love for them and the inclination of their nature toward them prevents them from denying them and from casting doubts upon them. Fourth: he is never free in any of his states from observing something among them and directly dealing with a portion of their kinds. And frequency of practice yields firm ability. And when you have recognized these aspects that necessitate the preponderance of this method over other methods, we say: since the matter is so, the divine books are filled with this type of proof, especially the Mighty Quran. Likewise, whenever you present many types of these proofs, hearts become pleased, souls become humbled, and thoughts become submissive to acknowledge the existence of the Wise God. And whoever seeks to investigate it fully, it is as if he cannot complete.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage explains why the proof from observable attributes (al-dalāʾil al-ḥissiyya) is superior to other types of proofs. The author states that this type is more impactful in hearts, more effective in minds, and further from doubts. He then gives four reasons (wujūh):

(1) Sensation (al-ḥiss) and imagination (al-khayāl) together act as two opposites to the intellect, thereby eliminating doubts. The idea is that such proofs are not purely abstract but involve direct sensory experience and imagination, which reinforce intellectual conviction.

(2) These proofs are numerous and diverse, and their abundance and continuous succession yield strength and certainty (al-quwwa wa-al-jazm). The multiplicity of instances reinforces conviction.

(3) These observed things, while being proofs in some respects, are also benefits in another respect. Humans are naturally disposed to love benefits, so their love and inclination prevent them from denying these proofs or casting doubts upon them.

(4) A person is never free from observing something among these proofs in any state and directly dealing with a portion of them. Constant practice (kathrat al-mumārasa) produces a firm habit (malaka rāsikha).

Having established these reasons, the author concludes that the divine books—especially the Quran—are filled with this type of proof. Presenting many such proofs causes hearts to become pleased, souls humbled, and thoughts submissive to acknowledge the existence of the Wise God. Whoever seeks to investigate this matter fully, it seems he cannot exhaust it.

Key Terms
أوقع في القلوب (awqaʿu fī al-qulūb)
الحس والخيال (al-ḥiss wa-al-khayāl)
القوة والجزم (al-quwwa wa-al-jazm)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first reason, what role do sensation and imagination play?
A) They are the same as intellect.
B) They act as two opposites to the intellect, dispelling doubts.
C) They are irrelevant to the proof.
D) They only create more doubts.

Key Takeaway
The first two reasons show that sensory proofs engage both sensory and rational faculties, and their abundance strengthens conviction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author says that abundance of proofs produces strength and certainty. Do you tend to rely on a single proof for your faith, or have you gathered multiple evidences? List three different proofs from creation that you have personally witnessed. If you can't, commit to seeking them out this week.
?
When you read this passage, do you feel your heart is impacted by the sensory proofs of Allah, or are you only convinced intellectually? Ask yourself: does my faith rest on abstract arguments or tangible signs? What change must I make to let the beauty of creation produce real certainty in my heart?

Benefits and Practice: The Third and Fourth Reasons
Author completes the enumeration of reasons and draws conclusion about divine books.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third and fourth reasons for the superiority of observable proofs: their appeal to human love of benefit and the firm habit from constant practice.

Core Idea
Observable proofs are also benefits, and constant engagement with them builds a firm habit of certainty.

Continuing from the previous lesson, the author gives two more reasons: the third is that these proofs are also benefits, which humans naturally love, preventing denial; the fourth is that constant practice yields a firm ability. He then concludes that divine books are filled with such proofs.

Guided Path

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم : أن هذا النوع من الدلائل أوقع في القلوب وأكثر تأثيرا في العقول ، وأبعد عن جهات الشبهات . والسبب فيه . وجوه : الأول : إن في هذا النوع من الدلائل الحس والخيال معا ضدان العقل فتزول الشبهات . والثاني : إنها كثيرة متعارضة بسبب الكثرة ، والتوالي يفيد القوة والجزم . والثالث : إن هذه الأشياء إن كانت دلائل من بعض الوجوه ، فإنها منافع من وجه آخر . والإنسان مجبول على حب المنافع . فكان حبه لها ، وميل طبعه إليها يمنعه من إنكارها، ومن إلقاء الشبهات فيها . والرابع : إنه لا ينفك في شيء من أحواله عن مشاهدة شيء فيها ، ومباشرة قسم من أقسامها . وكثرة الممارسة تفيد الملكة الراسخة . وإذا عرفت هذه الوجوه المقتضية لرجحان هذه الطريقة على سائر الطرق . فنقول : لما كان الأمر كذلك، كانت الكتب الإلهية مملوءة من هذا النوع من الدلائل . لا سيما القرآن العظيم. وكذلك فإنك متى أوردت أنواعاً كثيرة من هذه الدلائل، طابت القلوب ، وخضعت النفوس ، وأذعنت الأفكار ، للإقرار بوجود الإله الحكيم. ومن أراد الاستقصاء فيه . فكأنه لا يتم
And know: this type of proof is more impactful in hearts, more effective in minds, and further from the avenues of doubts. The reason for it has aspects: First: in this type of proof, sensation and imagination together are two opposites to the intellect, so doubts disappear. Second: they are numerous and diverse due to abundance, and succession yields strength and certainty. Third: these things, if they are proofs in some respects, they are benefits in another respect. And humans are naturally disposed to love benefits. So their love for them and the inclination of their nature toward them prevents them from denying them and from casting doubts upon them. Fourth: he is never free in any of his states from observing something among them and directly dealing with a portion of their kinds. And frequency of practice yields firm ability. And when you have recognized these aspects that necessitate the preponderance of this method over other methods, we say: since the matter is so, the divine books are filled with this type of proof, especially the Mighty Quran. Likewise, whenever you present many types of these proofs, hearts become pleased, souls become humbled, and thoughts become submissive to acknowledge the existence of the Wise God. And whoever seeks to investigate it fully, it is as if he cannot complete.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage explains why the proof from observable attributes (al-dalāʾil al-ḥissiyya) is superior to other types of proofs. The author states that this type is more impactful in hearts, more effective in minds, and further from doubts. He then gives four reasons (wujūh):

(1) Sensation (al-ḥiss) and imagination (al-khayāl) together act as two opposites to the intellect, thereby eliminating doubts. The idea is that such proofs are not purely abstract but involve direct sensory experience and imagination, which reinforce intellectual conviction.

(2) These proofs are numerous and diverse, and their abundance and continuous succession yield strength and certainty (al-quwwa wa-al-jazm). The multiplicity of instances reinforces conviction.

(3) These observed things, while being proofs in some respects, are also benefits in another respect. Humans are naturally disposed to love benefits, so their love and inclination prevent them from denying these proofs or casting doubts upon them.

(4) A person is never free from observing something among these proofs in any state and directly dealing with a portion of them. Constant practice (kathrat al-mumārasa) produces a firm habit (malaka rāsikha).

Having established these reasons, the author concludes that the divine books—especially the Quran—are filled with this type of proof. Presenting many such proofs causes hearts to become pleased, souls humbled, and thoughts submissive to acknowledge the existence of the Wise God. Whoever seeks to investigate this matter fully, it seems he cannot exhaust it.

Key Terms
المنافع (al-manāfiʿ)
جبلة (jibilla)
الملكة الراسخة (al-malaka al-rāsikha)
الكتب الإلهية (al-kutub al-ilāhiyya)
الإله الحكيم (al-Ilāh al-Ḥakīm)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fourth reason, what does frequent practice (kathrat al-mumārasa) produce?
A) Doubt and confusion.
B) Firm ability (al-malaka al-rāsikha).
C) Love of benefits.
D) Imagination.

Key Takeaway
The third and fourth reasons show that human nature and repeated practice reinforce belief, and the Quran extensively uses this approach.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter clear signs of God in your daily life, do you find yourself resisting them because they challenge your desires? How does your love for comfort or worldly benefits actually prevent you from acknowledging the truth that is right in front of you? What one step can you take today to let your love for truth outweigh your love for what is comfortable?
?
The author says that constant observation and practice builds a firm habit of certainty. Are you actively and consistently contemplating the signs of God in your life, or do you only think about God when you are in trouble? What specific practice will you commit to this week to build that firm ability of certainty?
?
The passage states that presenting many proofs leads hearts to be pleased, souls humbled, and thoughts submissive. Does your heart feel pleased when you study evidence for God's existence? If not, what is blocking your heart from experiencing that joy? What can you do to remove that block starting today?

The Four Compounds and Twofold Human Study
Author classifies compounds into four types and describes two approaches to studying humans.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author classifies created compounds into four types and how the study of humans reveals divine wisdom through two distinct approaches.

Core Idea
The universe is a book of signs: celestial, mineral, plant, animal, and especially human.

In this passage, the author begins by categorizing the tangible created world into four main types of compounds. He then zooms in on the human being, highlighting two complementary ways to study him. This classification sets the stage for his argument that such empirical evidence is uniquely powerful.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification of compounds
Read the Arabic passage carefully to identify the four types of compounds mentioned. Notice how the author includes humans within animals.
The author lists: celestial effects, minerals, plants, and animals—with humans in animals.
2
Understand the two ways to study humans
Focus on the sentence about humans: 'either concerning the dissection of his body... or concerning the dissection of the psychological faculties.' Reflect on why both are important.
This covers both physical anatomy and the inner faculties.
3
Reflect on the purpose of classification
Ask yourself: why does the author begin with this classification? How does it prepare us for the argument that follows about the effectiveness of this type of evidence?
The classification shows the breadth of evidence available.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيها من العجائب والمنافع. وأما المركبات فهي أربعة : الآثار العلوية والمعادن والنبات والحيوان والإنسان داخل في الحيوان . والبحث عن الإنسان، إما عن تشريح بدنه لمعرفة ما أودع الله فيه من الأسرار والعجائب والغرائب . وإما عن تشريح القوى النفسانية وأحوالها العجيبة من أنواع إدراكاتها وأفعالها. واعلم : أن هذا النوع من الدلائل أوقع في القلوب وأكثر تأثيرا في العقول، وأبعد عن جهات الشبهات . والسبب فيه وجوه : الأول : إن في هذا النوع من الدلائل الحس والخيال معا ضدان العقل فتزول الشبهات . والثاني : إنها كثيرة متعارضة بسبب الكثرة، والتوالي يفيد القوة والجزم . والثالث : إن هذه الأشياء إن كانت دلائل من بعض الوجوه ، فإنها منافع من وجه آخر . والإنسان مجبول على حب المنافع . فكان حبه لها، وميل طبعه إليها يمنعه من إنكارها، ومن إلقاء الشبهات فيها . والرابع : إنه لا ينفك في شيء من أحواله عن مشاهدة شيء فيها ، ومباشرة قسم من أقسامها . وكثرة الممارسة تفيد الملكة الراسخة . وإذا عرفت هذه الوجوه المقتضية لرجحان هذه الطريقة على سائر الطرق . فنقول : لما كان الأمر كذلك، كانت الكتب الإلهية مملوءة من هذا النوع من الدلائل . لا سيما القرآن العظيم. وكذلك فإنك متى أوردت أنواعا كثيرة من هذه الدلائل، طابت القلوب ، وخضعت النفوس ، وأذعنت الأفكار ، للإقرار بوجود الإله الحكيم. ومن أراد الاستقصاء فيه ، فكأنه لا يتم مقصوده إلا بشرح أسرار حكمة الله تعالى في جميع مخلوقاته ، وكل مبدعاته في عالمي الخلق والأمر ، وحشر الأجساد والأرواح . إلا أنا ننبه على معاقد هذه الأجناس والأنواع بحيث يصير الإنسان منها قادرا على التفريع والتفصيل . ومن الهداية والتوفيق .
In them are wonders and benefits. As for the compounds, they are four: the celestial effects, minerals, plants, and animals—and humans are included in animals. The study of humans is either concerning the dissection of his body to know what God has placed in it of secrets, wonders, and marvels, or concerning the dissection of the psychological faculties and their wondrous states from types of perceptions and actions. And know: this type of evidence is more effective in hearts, more influential in minds, and more remote from aspects of doubts. The reason for it has aspects: First: in this type of evidence, sense and imagination together are two opposites of the intellect, so doubts disappear. Second: they are many and varied due to multiplicity, and recurrence produces strength and certainty. Third: these things, if they are evidences in some respects, they are benefits in another respect. And the human is innately inclined to love benefits. So his love for them and the inclination of his nature towards them prevent him from denying them and from casting doubts upon them. Fourth: he is not free in any of his states from observing something in them and directly engaging with a part of their divisions. And frequent practice produces a firm habit. And when you know these aspects that necessitate the preponderance of this method over other methods, we say: Since the matter is so, the divine scriptures are filled with this type of evidence, especially the great Quran. Likewise, when you present many types of these evidences, hearts become pleased, souls become submissive, and thoughts become obedient to acknowledge the existence of the Wise God. And whoever desires to be exhaustive in it, it is as if his purpose cannot be completed except by explaining the secrets of the wisdom of God the Exalted in all His creations and all His originated things in the worlds of creation and command, and the gathering of bodies and souls. However, we point out the key points of these genera and species such that a person becomes capable of branching and detailing. And from [God] is guidance and success.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a combined classification and argumentation about the evidential power of created things. The author first classifies the compounds (المركبات)—the tangible created entities—into four types: celestial effects (الآثار العلوية, i.e., what is above the earth like stars and atmosphere), minerals, plants, and animals, noting that humans are included in the animal category. He then focuses on the study of humans, which can be approached in two ways: the anatomical dissection of the body to uncover the wonders God has placed within it, or the dissection of the psychological faculties (القوى النفسانية) and their amazing states of perception and action. After this classification, the author asserts that this type of evidence—i.e., empirical evidence from the created world—is more effective in hearts, more influential in minds, and more immune to doubts than other types of proofs. Then he provides four reasons for this superiority: (1) This evidence combines sense (الحس) and imagination (الخيال) which are both opposites of the intellect (العقل)—by engaging multiple faculties, doubts are removed. (2) The evidences are many and diverse, and their repetition (التوالي) engenders strength and certainty. (3) These things are not only evidences but also benefits (منافع) for humans; since humans are innately disposed to love benefits, their affection for these things prevents them from denying them or raising doubts about them. (4) A human is never free from observing some of these things and directly dealing with them in every situation; constant practice produces a firm habit of knowledge (الملكة الراسخة). Having established the preponderance of this method, the author concludes that this is why the divine scriptures, especially the Quran, are filled with this type of evidence. Presenting such varied signs softens hearts, humbles souls, and compels thoughts to acknowledge the existence of the Wise God. The author notes that to be exhaustive would require explaining all the secrets of God's wisdom in all creations, but his aim is to point out the key points (معاقد الأجناس والأنواع) so that one can branch out and elaborate further. The passage ends with a prayer for guidance and success.

المركبات
الآثار العلوية
المعادن
النبات
الحيوان
الإنسان
تشريح
القوى النفسانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Created compounds are four, and the study of humans covers both body and psychological faculties.

Four Reasons for the Superiority of Empirical Evidence
Author gives four reasons why empirical evidence from compounds is superior and concludes that scriptures are filled with such evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four reasons the author gives for why evidence from created compounds is more effective than other methods of proof.

Core Idea
Empirical evidence wins hearts because it engages sense, abundance, benefit, and constant observation.

After classifying compounds, the author argues that this type of evidence is the most convincing. He provides four distinct reasons that explain its unique power. Understanding these reasons helps us appreciate why divine scriptures are filled with such signs.

Guided Path
1
Read the four reasons
Read the Arabic passage from 'واعلم' to 'الملكة الراسخة'. Identify each reason as it begins with 'الأول', 'الثاني', etc.
The author uses numbered reasons (وجوه).
2
Understand each reason's logic
For each reason, reflect on how it contributes to making this evidence more effective. Think about why sense, multiplicity, benefit, and constant practice are persuasive.
Reason 1: sense & imagination vs intellect. Reason 2: multiplicity gives certainty. Reason 3: benefits appeal to human nature. Reason 4: constant observation builds habit.
3
See the conclusion
Read the concluding sentences: 'وإذا عرفت هذه الوجوه...' to the end. Notice how the author connects his reasoning to the divine scriptures, especially the Quran.
The conclusion reinforces the importance of empirical signs.

Proof from Human Generation: Diversity from Uniformity
The author presents a proof for God's existence based on human generation from sperm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author argues for the existence of a wise Creator by observing the diversity of human organs originating from a single sperm.

Core Idea
The diversity of our body points to a wise Creator, not blind chance.

The author presents a powerful proof from human biology. He observes that the human body is a marvel of complexity, with organs differing in size, shape, and texture, yet all derived from a simple sperm. This remarkable transformation, he argues, cannot be attributed to nature alone but demands a wise and merciful Designer. As we read, pay attention to the two possible explanations for the sperm's nature and the evidence from natural philosophers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main observation
Notice the author's starting point: the diversity of organs from a single source. This contrast sets up the proof.
The organs differ in quantity, shape, arrangement, hardness, and softness.
2
Understand the two views on sperm's composition
The author presents a dichotomy: either the sperm is truly uniform, or it appears uniform but is actually composed of parts from each organ. Grasp this distinction.
The latter view is held by many natural philosophers.
3
Examine the natural philosophers' arguments
They cite two pieces of evidence: universal pleasure during ejaculation and resemblance of offspring to parents. Reflect on how these support the heterogeneous view.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The proof implies that the formation of the human body from a simple sperm requires a wise and merciful agent, regardless of which view one accepts.
This is the core of the argument for the Wise, Merciful Being.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني والعشرون
الاستدلال على وجود الذكر الحكيم الرحيم بكيفية تولد الإنسان من النطفة
وتقرير هذا الدليل أن نقول : نرى أن بنية الأبدان مركبة من أعضاء مختلفة في المقدار والشكل ، والترتيب ، والصلابة ، والرخاوة . ثم إن هذه البنية اختلاف أجزاءها في الصفات والأحوال ، نراها متولدة من النطفة
ثم نقول : هذه النطقة إما أن تكون جسمها متشابه الأجزاء في نفس الأمر ، وإما [ أن يقال ] (١) إنه وإن كان متشابه الأجزاء بحسب الحس ، إلا أنه مختلف الأجزاء في الحقيقة وذلك لأن المني جسم ينفصل من ذوبان الأعضاء ، فينفصل من اللحم جزء [ حصلت ](۲) فيه الطبيعة اللحمية (۳) ، ومن العظم جزء حصلت فيه الطبيعة العظمية ، وكذا القول في جميع الأجزاء والأبعاض .
واعلم أن كثيرا من الطبيعيين ذهبوا إلى هذا القول ، واحتجوا على صحته بوجوه : -
الأول : عموم اللذة في جميع الأعضاء عند انفصال النطفة
والثانية : مشاكلة أعضاء المولود لأعضاء الوالدين في النقصان والزيادة
The twenty-second chapter: The argument for the existence of the Wise, Merciful Being through the manner of human generation from the sperm. And the exposition of this proof is that we say: We see that the structure of bodies is composed of organs differing in quantity, shape, arrangement, hardness, and softness. Then this structure—the variation of its parts in qualities and states—we see it generated from the sperm. Then we say: This sperm—either its body is homogeneous in parts in reality, or it is said that although it is homogeneous in parts according to sense perception, yet in reality it is heterogeneous in parts because semen is a body that separates from the dissolution of the organs, so from the flesh separates a part in which the fleshy nature came to be, and from the bone a part in which the bony nature came to be, and likewise for all parts and limbs. And know that many of the natural philosophers have adopted this view, and they argued for its validity by ways: The first: the universality of pleasure in all organs at the time of the separation of the sperm. And the second: the similarity of the organs of the newborn to the organs of the parents in deficiency and excess.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for the existence of God based on the generation of the human body from sperm. The author first states the observation: the human body is composed of diverse organs differing in quantity, shape, arrangement, hardness, and softness, yet it all originates from a simple sperm. This miraculous production from a uniform substance suggests a wise and merciful Creator. The author then discusses the nature of the sperm: either it is truly homogeneous, or it appears homogeneous to the senses but is actually composed of distinct parts corresponding to different organs. The latter view, held by many natural philosophers, posits that when the body dissolves, the sperm separates into parts carrying the nature of flesh, bone, etc. This is argued by two proofs: the universal pleasure felt in all organs during ejaculation (indicating that the sperm comes from all organs), and the similarity of the newborn's organs to the parents' organs (suggesting that the sperm carries the specific natures of the parents' organs). The author does not explicitly endorse either view here; rather, he presents the argument and the natural philosophers' reasoning as part of the broader proof for God's existence.

الذكر الحكيم الرحيم
النطفة
بنية الأبدان
متشابه الأجزاء
مختلف الأجزاء
الطبيعيون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The diversity of the human body can be explained by natural processes without a creator.
Correction: The author argues that the complexity and diversity arising from a simple sperm points to a wise Creator, not blind chance.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what main observation leads to the argument for the existence of God?
A) The diversity of organs in the body, all originating from a single sperm.
B) The pleasure felt in all organs during ejaculation.
C) The similarity of offspring to parents.
D) The dissolution of organs into sperm.

Key Takeaway
The transformation of a uniform sperm into a diverse body demonstrates the wisdom and mercy of the Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If the transformation from a drop of sperm to a complete human being testifies to Allah's mercy and power, then what does that mean for the way you treat this body? Does your gratitude reflect in your actions, or do you live as if it all happened by accident?
?
Right now, you are alive because a single cell grew into you. That process still continues—every cell, every breath, every beat. Does this realization make you humble before your Creator, or are you too absorbed in daily life to stop and ponder? What will you change today in response to this reality?

Two Opinions on Sperm Composition and Three Proofs for Heterogeneity
Sanusi presents two opinions on sperm composition and three proofs for heterogeneity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two competing views on the composition of sperm (homogeneous vs. heterogeneous) and the three proofs used by natural philosophers to argue for heterogeneity.

Core Idea
Sperm appears uniform but actually contains distinct components from every organ.

Sanusi begins the twenty-second chapter by presenting a remarkable observation: the diverse organs of the human body all originate from a single fluid. This leads to a debate among philosophers about whether sperm is truly homogeneous or contains hidden differences. The passage lays out both views and three empirical arguments for heterogeneity, setting the stage for a deeper theological argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how Sanusi sets up the observation and then presents the two opinions.
2
Identify the two opinions
Find where Sanusi states the two possibilities: either sperm is truly homogeneous, or it is only apparently homogeneous but actually heterogeneous.
The second opinion is the one defended by natural philosophers.
3
Examine the three proofs
The passage lists three proofs for heterogeneity. Read each one and understand how it supports the idea that sperm originates from all organs.
These proofs are based on pleasure, resemblance, and transmission of traits.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Sanusi concludes that the semen, though uniform to the senses, is actually composed of particles from each organ. Consider how this conclusion is used to argue for a wise Creator.
This conclusion is a premise for the larger argument for God's existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني والعشرون الاستدلال على وجود الذكر الحكيم الرحيم بكيفية تولد الإنسان من النطفة وتقرير هذا الدليل أن نقول : نرى أن بنية الأبدان مركبة من أعضاء مختلفة في المقدار والشكل والترتيب والصلابة والرخاوة . ثم إن هذه البنية اختلاف أجزاءها في الصفات والأحوال نراها متولدة من النطفة . ثم نقول : هذه النطفة إما أن تكون جسمها متشابه الأجزاء في نفس الأمر وإما [ أن يقال ] إنه وإن كان متشابه الأجزاء بحسب الحس إلا أنه مختلف الأجزاء في الحقيقة وذلك لأن المني جسم ينفصل من ذوبان الأعضاء فينفصل من اللحم جزء [ حصلت ] فيه الطبيعة اللحمية ومن العظم جزء حصلت فيه الطبيعة العظمية وكذا القول في جميع الأجزاء والأبعاض . واعلم أن كثيرا من الطبيعيين ذهبوا إلى هذا القول واحتجوا على صحته بوجوه : الأول : عموم اللذة في جميع الأعضاء عند انفصال النطفة . والثانية : مشاكلة أعضاء المولود لأعضاء الوالدين في النقصان والزيادة والكيفية . لأن المني لما انفصل من كل البدن كانت المشابهة حاصلة في كل البدن ولو كان المني لا ينفصل إلا من بعض الأعضاء وجب أن لا تحصل المشابهة إلا في تلك الأعضاء . والثالث : إنه لو حصل الخلل في عضو من أعضاء الوالدين فقد يحصل مثله في الولد وكذا القول في الشامات والعلامات الموجودة في جلد الوالدين فإنه يحصل في جلد الولد مثله فهذه الأحوال أمارات قوية توهم أن المني إنما انفصل من كل البدن لا من بعض أجزائه وعلى هذا القول فالجزء الذي ينفصل من اللحم ينعقد لحما والجزء الذي ينفصل من العظم ينعقد عظما وإذا عرفت هذا ظهر أن جرم المني وإن كان متشابه الأجزاء بحسب الحس إلا أنه مختلف الأجزاء في الحقيقة
The twenty-second chapter: The argument for the existence of the Reminder, the Wise, the Merciful, through the manner of the generation of man from the sperm-drop. And the presentation of this proof is that we say: We see that the structure of bodies is composed of organs differing in size, shape, arrangement, hardness, and softness. Then we see this structure, with its parts differing in qualities and states, generated from the sperm-drop. Then we say: This sperm-drop, either its body is homogeneous in parts in reality, or [it is said] that even if it is homogeneous in parts according to sense-perception, it is nevertheless heterogeneous in parts in reality, because the semen is a body that separates from the dissolution of the organs. So from the flesh separates a part in which the fleshy nature resides, and from the bone a part in which the bony nature resides, and likewise for all parts and limbs. And know that many of the natural philosophers have adopted this view and argued for its correctness with proofs: First: the generality of pleasure in all organs at the separation of the sperm-drop. Second: the resemblance of the limbs of the offspring to the limbs of the parents in deficiency, excess, and quality. For since the semen separates from the whole body, resemblance occurs in the whole body; but if the semen separated only from some organs, it would be necessary that resemblance occur only in those organs. Third: if a defect occurs in an organ of the parents, the like of it may occur in the offspring, and likewise for moles and marks present on the skin of the parents, for the like of them occurs on the skin of the offspring. So these states are strong indications suggesting that the semen separates from the whole body, not from some of its parts. And on this view, the part that separates from the flesh becomes flesh, and the part that separates from the bone becomes bone. And when you have understood this, it becomes apparent that the substance of the semen, even if it is homogeneous in parts according to sense-perception, is nevertheless heterogeneous in parts in reality.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage opens the twenty-second chapter, which aims to demonstrate the existence of God (here called al-dhikr al-ḥakīm al-raḥīm—the Reminder, the Wise, the Merciful) from the remarkable process of human generation from a sperm-drop. The author first lays out the basic observation: the human body is composed of diverse organs with different sizes, shapes, and textures, yet they all originate from what appears to be a single, uniform fluid. This leads to two possible views about the sperm-drop: either it is truly homogeneous in its internal parts, or it is only apparently homogeneous to the senses but actually composed of heterogeneous parts corresponding to the different organs it comes from. The latter view is defended by many natural philosophers (al-ṭabī‘iyyīn), who offer three proofs. The first proof is that pleasure is felt throughout the entire body during ejaculation, indicating that the semen originates from all organs. The second proof is that offspring resemble their parents in all their limbs, not just a few, which would not happen if the semen came from only some parts. The third proof is that congenital defects, moles, and skin marks in parents often reappear in their children, again pointing to a whole-body origin. The author concludes that the substance of semen, though seemingly uniform to the senses, is in reality a composite of particles from each organ. This sets the stage for the argument for a Creator that follows.

نطفة (sperm-drop)
مني (semen)
متشابه الأجزاء (homogeneous)
مختلف الأجزاء (heterogeneous)
طبيعيون (natural philosophers)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This passage is a scientific description of embryonic development.
Correction: Sanusi is using the empirical observations available in his time to build a theological argument for the existence of a wise Creator, not to conduct modern embryology.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Semen, though appearing uniform to the senses, is in reality composed of distinct particles from each organ, as argued by three empirical proofs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the pleasure proof: every part of your body was involved in the creation of the next generation. Does this fact change how you value your physical existence and its role in God's plan? What one action will you take today to honor that connection?
?
The resemblance proof shows that even small traits echo across generations. Look at your own family: what specific trait reminds you of your parents? How does that small, observable fact call you to thank the One who designed such precise continuity? Write down one way you will let this reflection affect your prayers today.
?
The third proof mentions defects and marks passing from parents to children. Have you ever considered that even imperfections in creation serve as signs of a wise Maker? How does this challenge your view of suffering or disability in yourself or others? What is one step you can take to see God's hand in the very things that seem flawed?

The Semen Argument for a Wise Creator
Sanusi argues from the formation of the body from semen, assuming homogeneity, to prove a Wise Creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the formation of the human body from seemingly homogeneous semen demonstrates the necessity of a Wise Creator, refuting purely naturalistic explanations.

Core Idea
Uniform causes cannot produce diversity; a Wise Maker must intervene.

Sanusi now presents a concrete proof from the generation of the human body. The argument begins by assuming the view that semen is homogeneous. If all natural forces act equally on a uniform substance, the result should be a uniform body. Yet the human body is strikingly diverse. This mismatch forces us to acknowledge a wise, intentional agent behind its formation. Additionally, philosophical principles about single powers and single matters further reinforce the need for a Creator.

Guided Path
1
Understand the assumption: semen is homogeneous
Read the passage's first premise: the body of semen is homogeneous in reality. This means all parts are identical in nature, and all natural forces act uniformly on it.
2
Trace the logical consequence of uniformity
If the recipient is homogeneous and the agent's influence is uniform, the effect must be uniform. So the human body should be uniform in nature, quality, and property.
3
Observe the contradiction with reality
The human body is not uniform; it has diverse organs and functions. This shows that natural forces alone cannot explain its formation.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Consider the philosophers' principle about spherical shape
A single power acting on a single matter necessarily produces a sphere. Since the human body is not spherical, a wise agent must have shaped it.
This is an additional proof from philosophical mechanics.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا عرفت هذا فاعلم أنا نذكر كيفية الاستدلال بتكون البدن من المني على وجود الصانع الحكيم على كل واحد من القولين . أما على القول بأن جسم المني مشابه للأجزاء في الحقيقة [ فتقرير الدليل : أن نقول : إن جسم المني متشابه الأجزاء في الحقيقة ] ونسبة حرارة الرحم والقوة الطبيعية [ وتأثيره بالطبائع ] والأنجم والأفلاك إلى جميع أجزاء ذلك المني على السوية . والقابل إذا كان متشابه الأجزاء كانت نسبة تأثير الفاعل إلى جميع تلك الأجزاء على السوية فعلى هذا التقدير يجب أن يكون الأثر متشابها [ وأن يكون الفعل متساويا ] وكان يجب أن يكون بدن الإنسان جسما متشابه الأجزاء من الطبع والصفة والخاصية ومعلوم أنه ليس كذلك . وأيضاً فمذهب الحكماء أن القوة الواحدة إذا عملت في المادة الواحدة وجب أن يكون الشكل الحاصل هو الكرة فكان يلزم أن يكون بدن الإنسان من جسم واحد متشابه الأجزاء في الطبيعة وأن يكون شكله هو الكرة
And when you have understood this, know that we mention the manner of argumentation from the formation of the body from the semen for the existence of the Wise Maker according to each of the two views. As for the view that the body of the semen is homogeneous in parts in reality, [the presentation of the proof is: that we say: The body of the semen is homogeneous in parts in reality,] and the ratio of the heat of the womb, the natural power, [and its influence upon the natures,] and the stars and the spheres, to all parts of that semen is uniform. And when the recipient is homogeneous in parts, the ratio of the effect of the agent to all those parts is uniform; so on this assumption, the effect must be uniform [and the action must be equal], and it would be necessary that the human body be a body homogeneous in parts in nature, quality, and property, and it is known that it is not so. Also, the doctrine of the philosophers is that a single power, when it acts upon a single matter, the resulting shape must be the sphere; so it would be necessary that the human body be from a single body homogeneous in parts in nature, and that its shape be the sphere.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage completes the argument by showing how the observed diversity of the human body, despite the apparent homogeneity of the semen, proves the existence of a Wise Maker (al-ṣāni‘ al-ḥakīm). The author assumes the first opinion (that semen is truly homogeneous) and draws the logical consequences. If the semen is uniform, then all the natural forces acting upon it—the heat of the womb, natural powers, stars, and spheres—affect it equally. Since the recipient (the semen) is homogeneous, the effect should be a completely uniform body, both in nature, quality, and property. Yet the human body is clearly diverse, with different organs and functions. This contradiction shows that natural forces alone cannot produce the human body; a wise, intentional agent must have intervened. The author then adds an additional argument from the philosophers (al-ḥukamā’): a single power acting on a single matter necessarily produces a spherical shape. If the semen were homogeneous and the only cause were natural, the human body should be a uniform sphere. Since it is not, naturalistic explanations fail, and the existence of a wise Creator is confirmed. The argument thus refutes materialistic accounts of human generation and points to divine design.

Key Terms

قوة واحدة
قابل
فاعل
كرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author denies natural causation entirely.
Correction: He does not deny natural causation; he argues that nature alone cannot fully explain the observed diversity, necessitating a wise Creator.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The formation of the human body from semen, given its diversity, cannot be the result of natural forces alone and thus proves the existence of a Wise Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your body is made of diverse parts—eyes, ears, heart, mind. Do you live as if each part was placed by a Wise Maker with a purpose, or do you treat your body as a collection of random matter to be used however you please? How will you honor that design today?
?
If the natural forces alone cannot produce even your physical form, how much less can they guide your soul? In what area of your life are you still trusting 'nature' or 'time' to fix what only the Wise Maker can mend? Make a specific commitment to turn to Him.
?
Sanusi argues that uniformity of cause should produce uniformity of effect. Look at the diversity in your own life—your abilities, circumstances, and trials. Do you see these as random outcomes or as the deliberate hand of a Wise Creator shaping you? What does that demand of you in gratitude and patience?

Two Arguments from Semen for a Wise Creator
Two arguments from semen for a wise Creator using two views on semen's composition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Razi uses two different views on semen (homogeneous and composite) to argue for a wise Creator, demonstrating that natural forces alone cannot produce the human body.

Core Idea
Nature cannot produce the orderly human body; only a wise Creator can.

This passage from a kalam work presents two arguments from the development of the human body from semen. Both arguments assume different natures of semen but lead to the same conclusion: the intricate structure of the body cannot be the result of blind natural forces, but must be the work of a wise Creator. By following the logic, you will see how theologians used observable biological facts to prove divine existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall argument structure.
Notice the two main sections marked by 'أما على القول' and 'وأما على القول'.
2
Analyze the first argument (homogeneous semen)
Identify the reductio ad absurdum: if semen is uniform and natural forces act equally, the body would be uniform and spherical. Since it is not, natural power cannot be the agent.
The argument uses a philosophical principle: one power acting on one matter produces a sphere.
3
Analyze the second argument (composite semen)
Examine the two aspects: (1) if semen is composite of simples, each simple would form a sphere, resulting in a spherical aggregate; (2) if semen is moist, nature cannot preserve order. The observed non-spherical, ordered body requires a wise Creator.
The second aspect highlights the failure of moist matter to maintain fixed positions, implying intelligent design.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا عرفت هذا، فاعلم أنا نذكر كيفية الاستدلال بتكون البدن من المني على وجود الصانع الحكيم، على كل واحد من القولين. أما على القول بأن جسم المني مشابه للأجزاء في الحقيقة [فتقرير الدليل: أن نقول: إن جسم المني متشابه الأجزاء في الحقيقة] ونسبة حرارة الرحم، والقوة الطبيعية [وتأثيره بالطبائع] والأنجم والأفلاك إلى جميع أجزاء ذلك المني على السوية. والقابل إذا كان متشابه الأجزاء كانت نسبة تأثير الفاعل إلى جميع تلك الأجزاء على السوية، فعلى هذا التقدير يجب أن يكون الأثر متشابها [وأن يكون الفعل متساويا] وكان يجب أن يكون بدن الإنسان جسما متشابه الأجزاء من الطبع والصفة والخاصية، ومعلوم أنه ليس كذلك. وأيضاً: فمذهب الحكماء أن القوة الواحدة إذا عملت في المادة الواحدة، وجب أن يكون الشكل الحاصل هو الكرة، فكان يلزم أن يكون بدن الإنسان من جسم واحد متشابه الأجزاء في الطبيعة، وأن يكون شكله هو الكرة، وحيث لم يكن [الأمر] كذلك علمنا أن المؤثرية في تكوين بدن الإنسان ليس هو القوة الطبيعية، بل الإله الحكيم الرحيم.

وأما على القول بأن جسم المني جسما مركبا من أجزاء مختلفة الطبائع [فنقول: تقرير هذا الدليل بناء على هذا القول من وجهين: الأول: كل مركب فإنه ينتهي تحلل تركيبه إلى البسائط، فإذا كان جسم المني مركبا من أجسام مختلفة الطبائع] فكل واحد من تلك الأجسام يجب أن يكون [جسما] بسيطا في نفسه، والقوة العاملة في تلك المادة البسيطة لا تقبل إلا شكلا متشابها، وهو الكرة، وحينئذ يلزم أن يكون جسم الإنسان مشكلا بشكل كرة، مضموم بعضها إلى البعض، ولما لم يكن الأمر كذلك، فقد فسد هذا القول.

والوجه الثاني: إن جسم المني جسم رطب، والجسم المرطب لا يحفظ وضع الأجزاء وترتيبها، فالجزء الذي يكون مادة للدماغ جزء مخصوص، والجزء الذي يكون مادة للقلب جزء آخر. وإذا كان الجسم الرطب لا يحفظ الوضع والترتيب، فلعل الجزء الذي هو مادة للقلب، يحصل فوق الجزء الذي هو مادة للدماغ، يحصل في الوسط. وحينئذ يجب أن يتولد ذلك الإنسان بحيث يصير قلبه فوق، ودماغه في الوسط، وحيث لم يكن الأمر كذلك [البتة] علمنا: أن حصول جواهر هذه الأعضاء، وحصول ما بها من الترتيب، إنما كان بتخليق إله قدير حكيم عليم، لا بتأثير الطبائع والأفلاك. فإن من لا يكون عليها حكيما امتنع أن تصدر عنه الأفعال المحكمة المتقنة [الموافقة للمصالح] وهذا دليل قوي كامل. ولقوة ظهوره، ذكره الله تعالى في
And if you know this, then know that we mention the manner of inference from the formation of the body from semen to the existence of the wise Maker, according to each of the two sayings. As for the saying that the body of semen is similar in parts in reality [the statement of the proof: we say: the body of semen is similar in parts in reality] and the proportion of the heat of the womb, and the natural power [and its effect by the natures] and the stars and the spheres to all parts of that semen is equal. And if the recipient is similar in parts, then the proportion of the effect of the agent to all those parts is equal. On this supposition, the effect must be similar [and the action must be equal], and the human body would have to be a body similar in parts in nature, quality, and property, and it is known that it is not so. Also: the doctrine of the philosophers is that when a single power acts on a single matter, the resulting shape must be the sphere. So it would follow that the human body consists of one body similar in parts in nature, and its shape would be the sphere. And since [the matter] is not so, we know that the effective agency in the formation of the human body is not natural power, but the wise, merciful God.

As for the saying that the body of semen is a composite body of parts differing in natures [we say: the statement of this proof based on this saying is from two aspects: first: every composite, its composition upon decomposition ends in simples. So if the body of semen is composed of bodies of differing natures], then each one of those bodies must be [a body] simple in itself, and the power working in that simple matter accepts no shape except a similar one, which is the sphere. Then it would follow that the human body is shaped as a sphere, with some parts attached to others. And since the matter is not so, this saying is refuted.

And the second aspect: the body of semen is a moist body, and a moist body does not preserve the position and arrangement of parts. So the part that is material for the brain is a specific part, and the part that is material for the heart is another part. And if the moist body does not preserve position and arrangement, then perhaps the part that is material for the heart occurs above the part that is material for the brain, [and that which is material for the brain] occurs in the middle. Then that human would be produced such that his heart is above and his brain is in the middle. And since the matter is not [at all] so, we know that the obtaining of the substances of these organs and the obtaining of the arrangement in them was only by the creation of a powerful, wise, knowing God, not by the effect of natures and spheres. For whoever is not wise over them is prevented from producing perfectly measured actions [conforming to interests]. And this is a strong, complete proof. And due to the strength of its clarity, God mentioned it in
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage presents two distinct arguments from the formation of the human body from semen to prove the existence of a wise Creator (الصانع الحكيم). The author begins by stating that he will show the method of inference according to two different views about semen: (1) that the body of semen is homogeneous in reality, and (2) that it is composite of parts with different natures. 

Under the first view (homogeneous semen), the author constructs a reductio ad absurdum. If semen is uniform, then the heat of the womb, natural power, stars, and spheres act equally on all parts. The recipient is uniform, so the effect should be uniform. Thus the human body would be uniform in nature, quality, and property, which it is not. Additionally, philosophers hold that a single power acting on a single matter produces a spherical shape. Therefore the human body would be a uniform sphere, but it is not. So the effective agent in forming the body cannot be natural power (القوة الطبيعية) but must be the wise, merciful God (الإله الحكيم الرحيم).

Under the second view (composite semen), the author presents two aspects. First, if semen is composed of different simple bodies, each simple body, when acted upon by a natural power, would produce a sphere. The whole body would then be a collection of spheres stuck together, which is not observed. Thus this view is refuted if one relies on natural causation. Second, semen is moist, and a moist body cannot preserve the fixed positions and order of parts. If left to nature, parts meant for the brain and heart could be interchanged, resulting in the heart above the brain. But the actual regular arrangement shows that an all-powerful, wise, knowing God (إله قدير حكيم عليم) created these organs with their proper order, not the natures and spheres. The author concludes that this proof is strong and complete, and due to its clarity, God mentioned it in the Quran (though the text cuts off).

Key Terms

صانع حكيم
قوة طبيعية
مركب
بسيط
كرة
تخليق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The arguments assume that semen is either fully homogeneous or fully heterogeneous, but the author uses both possibilities to lead to the same conclusion.
Correction: The author does not commit to either view; he shows that regardless of which view one takes, natural forces alone cannot produce the human body, thus proving a wise Creator.

Checkpoint
According to the first argument (assuming semen is homogeneous), what would necessarily result if natural forces alone were responsible for forming the human body?
A) The body would be uniform in nature and spherical in shape.
B) The body would have diverse organs like the brain and heart.
C) The body would be composed of multiple spheres stuck together.
D) The body would be moist and unable to preserve order.

Key Takeaway
Whether semen is homogeneous or composite, the intricate order of the human body cannot result from blind natural forces; it requires a wise Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage argues that natural forces alone cannot produce the intricate order of your body. When you look at your own hands, eyes, or brain, do you truly see them as the work of a wise Creator, or do you sometimes take them for granted as mere biology? How would your daily life change if you consciously viewed every part of your body as a divine gift?
?
If the consistent order in your body points to a wise Creator, why do you sometimes live as if your life is a product of random chance? What specific thought or action will you change today to remind yourself that you are created by a wise, merciful God?
?
The second argument shows that without a wise Creator, the parts of your body could be randomly arranged—your heart above your brain. Yet yours are perfectly placed. When you feel anxiety about your life's direction, do you trust that the same God who arranged your organs with precision is also arranging your circumstances? What is one area of your life you need to surrender to His wisdom?

The Spherical Shape Proof: From Composition to a Wise Creator
Sanusi presents the first proof from the composition of semen: simple elements would form spheres, but humans are not spheres.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the composition of semen into simple elements leads to the conclusion that a wise Creator must shape the human body, as natural forces would produce only spherical forms.

Core Idea
Natural forces can only produce spheres, but humans are not spheres, so a Wise Creator is needed.

In this passage, the author begins by asserting that natural power alone cannot account for the human body's formation. He then presents the first of two arguments based on the assumption that semen is composite. The argument shows that if semen were composed of simple elements, each would naturally take a spherical shape, yet the human body is not spherical, implying an intelligent shaper.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening assertion
Notice that the author states the conclusion before giving the proof. The passage begins by rejecting natural power as the agent and attributing it to God.
This sets the stage for the proof that follows.
2
Understand the composition premise
The proof assumes semen is composite of different natures. Every composite resolves into simple elements (basa'it). Grasp this logical move.
Simple elements are the building blocks.
3
Analyze the spherical shape consequence
A simple body's active power only produces a sphere. So if the human body came from simple elements, it would be spherical, but it is not. This contradiction refutes the naturalistic view.
4
Draw the conclusion
Since the body is not spherical, the composition premise must be false, or an external shaper intervenes. The argument leads to the necessity of a wise Creator.
The phrase 'فسد هذا القول' indicates refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحيث لم يكن الأمر كذلك علمنا أن المؤثرية في تكوين بدن الإنسان ليس هو القوة الطبيعية، بل الإله الحكيم الرحيم. وأما على القول بأن جسم المني جسماً مركبا من أجزاء مختلفة الطبائع فنقول: تقرير هذا الدليل بناء على هذا القول من وجهين: الأول: كل مركب فإنه ينتهي تحلل تركيبه إلى البسائط، فإذا كان جسم المني مركبا من أجسام مختلفة الطبائع فكل واحد من تلك الأجسام يجب أن يكون جسما بسيطا في نفسه، والقوة العاملة في تلك المادة البسيطة لا تقبل إلا شكلا متشابها، وهو الكرة، وحينئذ يلزم أن يكون جسم الإنسان مشكلا بشكل كرة، مضموم بعضها إلى البعض، ولما لم يكن الأمر كذلك، فقد فسد هذا القول. والوجه الثاني: إن جسم المني جسم رطب، والجسم الرطب لا يحفظ وضع الأجزاء وترتيبها، فالجزء الذي يكون مادة للدماغ جزء مخصوص، والجزء الذي يكون مادة للقلب جزء آخر. وإذا كان الجسم الرطب لا يحفظ الوضع والترتيب، فلعل الجزء الذي هو مادة للقلب، يحصل فوق الجزء الذي هو مادة للدماغ، يحصل في الوسط. وحينئذ يجب أن يتولد ذلك الإنسان بحيث يصير قلبه فوق، ودماغه في الوسط، وحيث لم يكن الأمر كذلك البتة علمنا: أن حصول جواهر هذه الأعضاء، وحصول ما بها من الترتيب، إنما كان بتخليق إله قدير حكيم عليم، لا بتأثير الطبائع والأفلاك. فإن من لا يكون عليها حكيما امتنع أن تصدر عنه الأفعال المحكمة المتقنة الموافقة للمصالح وهذا دليل قوي كامل. ولقوة ظهوره، ذكره الله تعالى في القرآن العظيم، في أكثر من ثمانين موضعا.
And since the matter is not so, we know that the effective agency in the formation of the human body is not natural power, but the Wise Merciful God. As for the view that the body of semen is a composite body composed of parts of different natures, we say: The presentation of this proof based on this view is from two aspects: First: Every composite, when its composition is analyzed, ends in simple elements. So if the body of semen is composed of bodies of different natures, then each one of those bodies must be a simple body in itself, and the active power in that simple matter accepts only a uniform shape, which is the sphere. Then it would be necessary that the human body be formed as a sphere, with its parts pressed together. And since it is not so, this view has been refuted. The second aspect: The body of semen is a moist body, and the moist body does not preserve the position and order of parts. The part that becomes matter for the brain is a specific part, and the part that becomes matter for the heart is another part. And if the moist body does not preserve position and order, perhaps the part that is matter for the heart comes to be above the part that is matter for the brain, and the brain comes to be in the middle. Then it would be necessary that that human be generated such that his heart is above and his brain in the middle. And since it is not so at all, we know that the attainment of the substances of these organs and the attainment of the order they have came about only through the creation of a Powerful, Wise, Knowing God, not through the influence of natures and celestial spheres. For one who is not wise over them cannot produce precise, perfect actions that are suited to benefits. And this is a strong, complete proof. And due to the strength of its clarity, God mentioned it in the Mighty Qur'an in more than eighty places.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage presents two proofs for the existence of a wise Creator based on the assumption that semen is a composite body. The author first concludes that the formation of the human body cannot be attributed to natural power but to God. Then, assuming the composition of semen, two arguments are given. The first argues that if semen is composite, its components are simple and each would produce spherical shapes, but the human body is not spherical, so the assumption fails, implying an external ordering agent. The second argument points out that semen is moist and cannot maintain the precise arrangement of parts (e.g., brain matter vs. heart matter); if left to nature, they would be disordered, but actual order proves a wise Creator. The author emphasizes that such precise design cannot come from a non-wise agent and notes that the Qur'an mentions this proof in over eighty places.

?

?

?
Sanusi's proof forces a choice: either your existence is a product of mindless nature (and you would be a sphere) or of a Wise God. Which do you truly believe, and if you believe in God, why do you still live as if your life is random and purposeless? What is one thing you will change today to align your life with the purpose your Creator intended?

The Moist Body Proof: Order Requires a Wise Creator
Sanusi presents the second proof: the moist nature of semen cannot preserve organ order, so a wise Creator must impose it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the moist and unordered nature of semen leads to the conclusion that only a wise Creator could give the body its precise organ arrangement.

Core Idea
Moist matter cannot hold order, so the body's precise arrangement proves a wise Designer.

The second proof focuses on the moist nature of semen. The author argues that a moist body cannot preserve the positions and order of parts. If left to natural forces, the parts designated for different organs would become randomly arranged, leading to absurd possibilities like the heart being above the brain. Since the actual arrangement is orderly and functional, there must be a wise Creator who imposed this order.

Guided Path
1
Understand the premise
Semen is a moist body, and moist bodies cannot preserve the position and order of parts. Moisture causes instability; parts can shift.
2
Identify the parts
Different parts of semen are destined for different organs (brain, heart, etc.). The matter for the brain is distinct from matter for the heart.
These parts are specific substances.
3
Consider the consequence
If the moist body cannot hold order, the parts could swap positions, leading to a body with heart above brain. This would be a chaotic outcome.
The author suggests this as a possibility.
4
Contrast with reality
The actual human body has the heart below the brain, so the arrangement is not random. This implies an external ordering agent.
5
Conclude the proof
The precise order must come from a Powerful, Wise, Knowing God. The author emphasizes that a non-wise being cannot produce precise, beneficial actions.
The proof is strong and mentioned frequently in the Qur'an.

Two Objections to the Proof from Semen and Partial Refutation
Two objections and partial refutation of the second.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two naturalistic objections to the argument from the formation of organs in the womb and the beginning of a refutation that focuses on the impossibility of a blind generative power producing intricate design.

Core Idea
Biological processes of human formation cannot be explained by blind forces – they require an intelligent cause.

This passage presents two objections that skeptics might raise against the teleological argument from the development of the human embryo. The first suggests that specific properties in the uterus determine organ formation, while the second posits a special generative power in the semen. The author begins to dismantle the second objection by showing that such a power would need to possess knowledge and power beyond what is observed, thus pointing to a higher cause.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the flow of the argument. Notice that the passage is incomplete and cuts off mid-sentence.
The passage is from page 222 and continues in the next lesson.
2
Identify the two objections
Find the two objections: the first about specific properties of the uterus, the second about a generative power in the semen. Note how they attempt to explain the formation of organs without invoking a creator.
The second objection is given more attention and is the focus of the partial refutation.
3
Analyze the refutation of the second objection
The author divides the claim of a generative power into two possibilities: either it has knowledge and power to choose the best arrangement, or it is completely devoid of awareness. The first possibility is rejected because such a power would effectively be divine.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum argument.
4
Consider the argument's implication
Reflect on why the author says that even the perfect human soul cannot create such a body, so the generative power in the semen cannot either. This leads to the conclusion that only a transcendent cause can account for the complexity.
The argument is incomplete but sets the stage for the full refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: السؤال عليه من وجوه: الأول: لم لا يجوز أن يقال: إن كل واحد من أجزاء الرحم مخصوص بخاصية لأجلها، توجب حدوث الكيفية المخصوصة في الجزء الذي يتصل به من المني، فيكون تولد الأعضاء المختلفة لهذا السبب؟ وهي السؤال الثاني: لم لا يجوز أن يقال: حل في جسم المني قوة مخصوصة، المسماة بالقوة المولدة، وتلك القوة المولدة هي التي أفادت هذه الآثار المختلفة وفعلت هذه الآثار العجيبة؟ فإن قالوا: هذا محال لأن هذه القوة الحالة في جسم المني، المسماة بالقوة المولدة، إما أن يكون لها علم بوجود المنافع والمصالح وقدرة على تحصيل الوجه الأصلح الأصوب من التركيبات الموافقة وإما أن يقال: هذه القوة قوة لا شعور لها بشيء ولا قدرة لها على تحصيل شيء، بل هي قوة خالية عن الشعور والإدراك. أما القسم الأول: فهو باطل. إذ لو كان الأمر كذلك، لكانت تلك القوة عالمة بوجود المنافع والمصالح، والمضار، والمفاسد، وقادرة على تحصيل المنافع، ودفع المضار، ولكانت هي التي خلقت هذا البدن، وركبت هذه البنية على هذا التركيب العجيب، والتأليف الغريب، لكنا نعلم بالضرورة أنه ليس الأمر كذلك لأن القوى البدنية، والنفس الإنسانية في حال كمال العقل، وفي حال كمال البدن أكمل حالا ما كانت في أول الأمر حال ما كان البدن نطفة، فلما لم تقدر النفس الإنسانية حال كمالها على شيء من هذه الأحوال، ففي الحالة التي كانت في غاية النقصان والتصور. كيف يعقل أن يقال: إنها
If it is said: The objection to it is from [several] aspects: First: Why is it not permissible to say that each one of the parts of the uterus is specified by a property due to which it necessitates the occurrence of the specific quality in the part of the semen that connects to it, so that the generation of different organs occurs for this reason? And it is the second question: Why is it not permissible to say that there resides in the body of semen a specific power, called the generative power (al-quwwa al-muwallida), and that generative power is what conferred these different effects and performed these wondrous effects? For if they say: This is impossible because this power residing in the body of semen, called the generative power, either has knowledge of the existence of benefits and interests and the ability to attain the most correct and most suitable arrangement from the compatible compositions, or it is said: This power is a power that has no awareness of anything and no ability to attain anything, but rather it is a power empty of sentience and perception. As for the first division, it is false. For if it were so, that power would be knowing of the existence of benefits and interests, harms and corruptions, and able to attain benefits and repel harms, and it would be the one that created this body and composed this structure upon this wondrous composition and strange arrangement, but we know by necessity that it is not so because the bodily powers and the human soul, in the state of perfect intellect and in the state of perfect body, are more complete than they were in the first state when the body was a drop. Since the human soul in its state of perfection is not capable of any of these states, then in the state that was in extreme deficiency and [incomplete] formation, how can it be said that it ...
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage presents two objections to the proof from semen and begins the refutation of the second. The first objection suggests that each part of the uterus has a specific property that determines the formation of different organs from the semen. The second objection posits a generative power (al-quwwa al-muwallida) in the semen that produces the different organs. The author then refutes the second objection by dividing the generative power into two possibilities: either it has knowledge and power to choose the best arrangement, or it is devoid of awareness and ability. The first possibility is dismissed because if true, that power would be all-knowing and all-powerful, effectively God, which is not observed since even the perfect human soul cannot create such a body. Therefore, the generative power cannot be the cause. The text cuts off during the explanation, but the argument is that a power without awareness cannot produce such precise order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that specific properties in the uterus or a generative power in the semen are sufficient to explain the formation of organs without a creator.
Correction: The author argues that any explanation based on blind forces fails because such forces lack the necessary knowledge and power to produce the intricate design; only a transcendent, intelligent cause can account for it.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the problem with the claim that a generative power in the semen produces the different organs?
A) The generative power is not strong enough to shape organs.
B) The generative power would have to be all-knowing and all-powerful to choose the best arrangements, but that is not observed.
C) The generative power only works in the uterus, not in the semen.
D) The generative power is a natural force that works without any knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Neither bodily properties nor a blind generative power can account for the intricate design of the human body; a higher intelligence must be the cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you honestly reflect on the intricate design of your own body—from the formation of your organs to their coordinated functions—do you find yourself more inclined to attribute it to blind chance or to a wise Creator? What in your daily life reveals that tendency?
?
The author argues that even the perfected human soul cannot create such a structure. How does this truth challenge your sense of self-sufficiency? In what specific areas of your life do you still act as if you are the ultimate cause of your own success or well-being?
?
When you consider that the process of your own creation was beyond your awareness and control, does it humble you? If so, how can you cultivate a deeper daily awareness of your dependence on the One who designed you?
